## 7.22 REHEATERS

The superheaters discussed above which superheat the saturated steam just produced in the boiler are known as primary superheaters. The reheaters, also known as intermediate (or reheat) superheaters, in which the worked-off steam returned form the turbine is again superheated.

As discussed in earlier chapters, reheat cycles need two or more stages of superheating, one for turbine throttle steam and one or more for steam taken from the turbine for re-superheating. This is done for taking full advantage of the improved cycle efficiency offered by the high steam pressure and also avoid excessive wetness at the low pressure end of the turbine.

In the reheaters, the steam is withdrawn from the turbine before it becomes saturate during expansion and is reheated before passing back to the turbine to complete its expansion. In the reheater, steam comes from the high-pressure turbine and after being reheated it goes to the intermediate-pressure turbine for further expansion.

The type of reheaters installed are very similar to those of the superheater, the only difference being in the use, generally, of a slightly larger tube size. The modern units have reheaters in the same gas passages of the boiler as the superheaters.

The reheaters should be designed to avoid large pressure drops. Use of higher reheat pressure results in reduced steam volume and economical tube size, although theoretically lower reheat pressures are conductive to greater cycle efficiency.

Since the reheaters have lower pressure as compared to the superheaters, the stresses are lower and hence a lower grade steel alloy can be used. The reheater is usually located above the primary or convective superheater in the convective zone of utility boilers.

## 7.23 HEAT FLOW

A power plant consists mainly of equipment for energy flow and transformation. The basic modes of heat transfer are as follows.

(a) Conduction (b) Convention

(c) Radiation.

All the three forms of heat transfer are found in power plant engineering usually in combination with each other. The principal heat transfer calculations are associated with the following:

(i) Radiation from fuel bed and luminous gases to boiler tubes and water walls.

(ii) Radiation and conduction in heat insulators like refractories and pipe coverings.

(iii) Conduction of heat through boiler, economiser and air preheater surfaces.

(iv) Conduction of heat through condenser or heater tubes.

(v) Heat convection from combustion region to more remote boiler tubes, economiser tubes and air preheater surfaces.

## 7.24 BOILER PERFORMANCE

The performance of a steam boiler may be expressed in terms of the following:

(i) Heat release per cubic metre of furnace volume.

(ii) Efficiency.

(iii) Heat transferred per square metre of the heating surface area per hour.

(iv) Rate of combustion in kcal per square metre of the grate area per hour for solid fuel.

(v) Amount (kg) of steam produced per hour.

## Equivalent Evaporation

To compare evaporative capacity or performance of different boilers working under different conditions it is desirable to provide a common base so that water be supposed to be evaporated under standard conditions.

The standard conditions adopted are temperature of feed water ${ 1 0 0 ^ { \circ } C }$ and converted into dry and saturated steam at 100°C. As per these standard conditions 1 kg of water at $1 0 0 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { C }$ requires 2257 kJ to get converted to steam at $1 0 0 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { C }$

Therefore equivalent evaporation is defined as the amount of water evaporated from water at $1 0 0 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { C }$ to dry and saturated steam at $1 0 0 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { C } .$ . However (i) the evaporation rate of boiler may also be expressed in terms of kg of steam per kg of fuel.

(ii) The capacity of a boiler may also be expressed in terms of total heat added per hour.

Factor of evaporation (Fe)

It is defined as follows

$$
F e = \frac { H _ { 1 } } { H _ { 2 } }
$$

where $H _ { 1 } =$ Heat received by 1 kg of water under working conditions.

H = Heat received by one kg of water evaporated from and at $1 0 0 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { C }$

## Heat losses in a boiler plant

The heat losses which may take place in a boiler plant are as follows:

(i) heat loss due to incomplete combustion of fuel

(ii) heat loss due to unburnt fuel

(iii) convection and radiation heat loss

(iv) heat lost in flue gases.

## Boiler Trial

Steam is generated in boilers under certain conditions of inlet water and exist steam while a certain rate of fuel is being burnt. In order to study the performance of boiler the experiments are conducted by operating the boiler for a certain length of time and recording the data. This procedure is known as boiler trial. A heat balance sheet is prepared which indicates the heat supplied, heat utilised through various sources and heat wasted.

The main objects of boiler trial are as follow:

(i) To determine the thermal efficiency of the boiler when working at a definite pressure.

(ii) To draw up heat balance sheet for the boiler to check the performance of the boiler.

## Heat Loss in Boilers

The various causes of heat loss in a boiler are as follows:

(i) Loss due to heat carried away in chimney gases.

(ii) Loss due to incomplete combustion of fuel. This can be due to insufficient air supply or fuel bed being in poor conditions.

(iii) Loss due to moisture formed by combustion of hydrogen in fuel.

(iv) Loss due to moisture in coal.

(v) Loss due to radiation and convection from boiler.

(vi) Heat loss due unburnt fuel which is passed on to the ash pit.

## Thermal Efficiency of Boiler

Thermal efficiency of a boiler is defined as the ratio of heat actually utilised by water in generation of steam to the heat supplied during combustion of fuel.

$$
\eta _ { \mathrm { { B o i l e r } } } = { \frac { W { \left( { H _ { \mathrm { { 2 } } } } - H _ { \mathrm { { 1 } } } \right)}  } { W _ { \mathrm { { 1 } } } \times C V } }
$$

where W = Weight of steam produced, kg

H<sub>1</sub> = Enthalpy of feed water, kcal/kg

H<sub>2</sub> = Total heat of steam, kcal/kg at the generation pressure

W<sub>1</sub> = Weight of fuel burnt, kg

C.V. = Calorific value of fuel, kcal/kg.

Although the major portion of heat produced during combustion of fuel is utilised to heat the feed water for conversion into steam but some portion of heat produced is lost in flue gases leaving the chimney and some amount of heat is lost due to radiation from furnace to the outside. The boiler efficiency is nearly 75% without heat recovery equipment and it varies from 85 to 90% with heat recovery equipment.

Boiler performance can be improved by taking into account the following factors:

(i) Proper supervision should be carried out.

(ii) Too much excessive air should not be supplied.

(iii) Boiler, superheater, economiser and air heater surfaces should be cleaned at proper intervals.

(iv) Type of fuel used also controls boiler efficiency. Fig. 7.52 compares the performance in burning bituminous coal, oil or natural gas in the boiler.

![](images/e2415eb16ea4bdf584ad8b3daf8bd228878977af10f1593137234ff3c8124941.jpg)

Efficiency of a boiler depends on the following factors:

(i) Steam pressure

(ii) Calorific value

(iii) Effectiveness in burning of fuel.

Indication of the effective burning of fuel is given by the percentage of the carbon dioxide $\mathrm { ( C O _ { 2 } ) }$ in the flue gases. The percentage of $\mathrm { { C O } _ { 2 } }$ to give maximum efficiency and satisfactory operation will depend on:

(a) type of fuel such as oil, gas, coal.

(b) method of firing.

(iv) Capacity of boilers

(v) Use of heat recovery apparatus such as air preheater, economiser etc.

## Ways of Increasing Thermal Efficiency.

The thermal efficiency of a steam power plant can be increased by the following ways :

(i) An increase in the initial pressure of steam raises the thermal efficiency.

(ii) The thermal efficiency can be increased by raising the initial temperature of the steam without changing the pressure.

(iii) Intermediate reheating of steam improves the thermal efficiency of the plant. As already mentioned an increase in the initial pressure of steam improves the thermal efficiency steam power plant but the wetness fraction of such steam also grows at the end of expansion. The wetness is so high that it causes wear of the blades of the last

stages of a steam turbine. This shortcoming is eliminated by intermediate reheating of the steam. The steam from boiler after partial expansion in the first stage turbine is fed into super heater, where it is reheated at a constant pressure either to the temperature of live steam or to a temperature slightly below that one. The reheated steam then flows to the last stages of the turbine where the process of expansion is completed (Fig. 7.53).

![](images/3e8cfa86e1b79db5151f7d3a9c02c4b98540ba64b4230b0f0c118cc1c4fcb268.jpg)

    - The feed pump circulates this water back to the boiler.

This process diagram illustrates a basic thermal power plant cycle.
      
Fig. 7.53. Reheating of the steam

(iv) Thermal efficiency of steam power plant can be improved by carrying out regenerative heating of the feed water. Such heating of the water is carried out by using the heat of steam partly tapped from the turbine. In this method (Fig. 7.54) the steam from boiler flows into steam turbine. After partial expansion some of the steam is tapped from the first stage of the turbine and directed to feed water heater and then to feed tank. The remaining steam enters the second stage of the turbine where it continues to expand. At the outlet from the second stage some of the steam is directed into water heater and then to feed tank. The other part of steam goes to the third stage of the turbine and expands there to the final pressure and enters the condenser. The condensate is delivered by pump to feed tank.

Example 7.5 Determine the boiler efficiency if the boiler generate 23,000 kg of steam at 10.2 kg/cm2 dry and saturated. The amount of coal used is 2100 kg and the calorific value of coal is 8600 kcal/kg. The feed water temperature is $1 0 5 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { C }$

Solution. The heat of steam at 10.2 kg/cm2 = 664 kcal/kg

$$
\eta _ { \mathrm { B o l i e r } } = { \frac { 2 3 , 0 0 0 { \left( 6 6 4 - 1 0 5 \right) } } { 2 1 0 0 \times 8 6 0 0 } } = 0 . 7 1 = 7 1 \% { \bf A } { \bf n } { \bf s }
$$

## 7.25 BOILER INSPECTION AND MAINTENANCE

1. Boiler Inspection. The boiler are required to be tested regularly as per Indian Boilers Act. Before inspection, boiler should be made empty and all manhole doors, caps, mud drums, fire bars, fire arches, front end bridge plates, oil burners should be removed and boiler should be cleaned. All tubes, smoke boxes and external flues should be cleaned and checked. All the steam and water connections should be disconnected and then it should be made ready for conducting the following tests.

(a) Hydraulic Test. For this test, the mountings should be fitted tightly except the safety valves. The openings of the safety valves should be closed. All the joints should be made tight. Boiler is filled with water and inspectors gauges should be fitted to the boiler. Generally the boilers is tested at twice the working pressure of the boiler. During this test no part of boiler should deflect.

(b) Steam Test. This test is conducted to check whether the safety valves operate properly to relieve the steam when the steam pressure inside the boiler exceeds the rated pressure. This operation is tested keeping the feed valve and steam stop valve closed.

2. Boiler Maintenance. Regular maintenance and careful supervision of working of various components of boiler result in the efficient operation of the boiler. The various factors which should be carefully observed for proper maintenance of the boiler are as follow:

1. The combustion equipment should be so adjusted that the temperature in the furnace does not exceed the designed value. The air supply to the furnace should be in correct proportion.

2. The water level in the boiler should not be allowed to fall beyond the minimum level.

3. The temperature should change slowly and uniformly in the various parts of the boiler. Rapid changes in temperature cause unequal expansion.

4. The water used for steam generation should be free from scale forming impurities because the scale if deposited on tube and boiler shell does not allow the heat transfer to take place effectively and sometimes causes over heating of tubes and boiler shell which may result in tubes failure and boiler explosion.

5. Soot and ash deposited in tubes on gas side should be removed regularly.

6. Bearings of pumps, stokers, pulverisers and fans, etc., should be lubricated regularly.

7. Oil or scale in the tubes is undesirable, hence such tubes should be located and problem is removed.

8. All stays should be in even tension and they should be properly adjusted.

9. The tube leakage is caused due to blistering of tubes as it is exposed to high temperature. The boiler should be stopped when such leakage is noted and it must be immediately repaired.

## 7.25.1 Boiler Tube Failure and Prevention

With the introduction of 200 and 500 MW capacity boiler, the outages of boilers due to tube leakage vary from 10 to 15% of the total outages. Therefore, it is necessary to combate this problem in the initial stages. The basic causes of the tube failures are corrosion, stress cracking, thermal fracture, stress rupture and creep distortion.

When the water and steam chemistry are not maintained within the limits recommended by the boiler manufacturer, corrosion or corrosion related damage may occur in feedwater heaters, economiser, and water wall. Over-heating damage may also occur in these tubes as well as in superheater and reheater tubes, if deposits are build up in them due to poor water treatment and improper boiler operation. Overheating of the boiler tubes is the main cause of their failure.

The problem of corrosion have already been discussed while dealing with feedwater treatment in earlier sections. The outer surface erosion of the water tubes is caused by an erosive action of ash particles in the gases. Erosion is enhanced by high flue gas velocities. Erosion creates spots, wall thinning and finally tube failure. These can be reduced upto some extent by controlling the excess air supplied to the combustion chamber, and by providing baffles, and tube shields can be welded in the maximum affected zones.

## 7.26 MODERN TRENDS IN BOILERS

1. In modern boilers, water wall (water-cooled furnace walls) eventually led to the integration of furnace, economiser, boiler, superheater, reheater and air preheater.

2. One boiler per turbine is provided to simplify the piping system and the use of steam reheating.

3. No drum is provided in boilers operating at pressures above the critical pressure (221 bar) since no separation of the water and steam occurs. The water enters the bottom of the tubes and is completely transformed to steam by the time it reaches the top, passing through the tubes only once. Therefore, these are known as a oncethrough boiler (also referred as drumless boiler).

4. A large number of steam generation units are designed to work in the ranges of 125 bar and 510°C to 300 bar and 600°C which are basically characterised as sub-critical and super-critical. Usually a sub-critical boiler consists of three distinct section as economiser, evaporator and superheater and in case of super critical boiler the only economiser (preheater) and superheater are required.

5. The most recent method to produce economical thermal power is by the use of supercritical cycle. It is a general practice to use super-critical boilers above 300 MW capacity units, as super-critical boilers have higher thermal efficiency, least problems of corrosion and erosion, and are easy to operate. Presently, about 250 bar and 540°C are used for 500 MW capacity units.

6. Use of supercharged boilers are also becoming common, in which the combustion is carried out under pressure in the combustion chamber by supplying the compressed air. In this, in addition to generating steam in the boiler for use in turbine like other boilers, the exhaust gases from the combustion chamber are used to run gas turbine as they are exhaust at high pressure. The part of the gas turbine output can be used to drive other auxiliaries.

7. Modern boilers have sufficiently large furnace to complete combustion of fuel and contain enough heat transfer surface in suitable arrangement, to prevent excessive slagging on the water walls and tubes.

(ii) Coal consumption per day.

$$

$$

assuming maximum demand equal to capacity of the power station.

Average load

$$
\mathbf { \delta } = 0 . 5 \times 4 0 \times 1 0 0 0 = 2 0 , 0 0 0 \mathrm { { k W } }
$$

Energy produced per day = Average load × 24 = 20,000 × 24 = 48 × 10<sup>4</sup> kWh.

Overall thermal efficiency $= { \frac { 8 6 0 } { W \times 6 8 0 0 } }$

$$

$$

$$

= { \frac { 1 } { 0 . 9 0 } } = 1 . 1 1 \mathrm { { k W h } }

Energy output per day = 18 × 105 kWh

$$

Example 7.11. The following data is supplied for a boiler plant:

$$

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l } & { = { \cfrac { H } { H _ { 1 } } } \times 1 0 0 } \\ & { = { \cfrac { 1 3 0 4 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } } { 1 5 8 4 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } } } \times 1 0 0 \ = 8 2 . 3 \% \quad { \mathrm { A n s } } . } \end{array} }
$$

This shows that by installing economiser the efficiency of the boiler plant is increased.

Example 7.12 Determine the quantity of air required per kg of coal burnt in a steam power plant furnace fitted with a 62 m high stack. The draft produced is 38 mm of water and tempera ture of flue gases is 410°C. Boiler house temperature is 29°C.

Solution.

$$
h = { \mathrm { D r a u g h t } } = 3 8 { \mathrm { ~ m m ~ o f ~ w a t e r } }
$$

W = Weight of air required per kg of coal burnt

T<sub>1</sub> = Absolute temperature of air outside the chimney

T = Average absolute temperature of chimney (stack) gases.

$$
= 4 1 0 + 2 7 3 = 6 8 3 ^ { \circ } \mathrm { K }
$$

$$
H = \mathrm { H e i g h t ~ o f ~ c h i m n e y } = 6 2 ~ \mathrm { m } .
$$

$$
h = 3 5 3 H \left[ \frac { 1 } { T _ { 1 } } - \left( \frac { W + 1 } { W } \right) \times \frac { 1 } { T } \right]
$$

$$
3 8 = 3 5 3 \times 6 2 \biggl [ \frac { 1 } { 3 0 2 } - \biggl ( \frac { W + 1 } { W } \biggr ) \times \frac { 1 } { 6 8 3 } \biggr ]
$$

$$

Example 7.13 In a steam power plant an endless rope haulage raises 300 tonnes of coal through a vertical distance of 80 metres in one hour. If the efficiency of the haulage system is 40% and the system runs for 8 hours per day for 5 days, calculate the following:

(a) H.P. output of system

(b) Power input

(c) Weekly cost of coal raising. The charge for electricity is Rs. 2.00 paise per kWh.

Solution.

$$
t = { \mathrm { T i m e } } = 1 { \mathrm { h o u r } } = 3 6 0 0 { \mathrm { s e c } } .
$$

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l } & { P = { \mathrm { P o w e r ~ o u t p u t } } } \\ & { \quad = { \mathrm { m g h } } = 3 0 0 \times 1 0 0 0 \times 9 . 8 \times 8 0 } \\ & { \quad = 2 3 5 2 \times 1 0 ^ { 5 } { \mathrm { J } } } \\ & { \quad = { \frac { 2 3 5 2 \times 1 0 ^ { 5 } } { t } } = { \frac { 2 3 5 2 \times 1 0 ^ { 5 } } { 3 6 0 0 } } = 6 5 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } W } \end{array} }
$$

(As 1 W = 1 J per sec)

Power output (H.P.)

$$
{ \bf \Omega } = { \frac { 6 5 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } } { 7 3 5 . 5 } } = { \bf 8 8 } { \bf A n s } .
$$

$$
\eta \ = \mathrm { E f f i c i e n c y } = 0 . 4
$$

Power input

$$
{ \bf \Omega } = \frac { 8 8 } { 0 . 4 } = { \bf 2 2 0 H . P . } \qquad { \bf A n s . }
$$

$$
= 8 \times 5 = 4 0
$$

Power input

$$
= { \frac { \mathrm { P o w e r ~ o u t p u t } } { \eta } } = { \frac { 6 5 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } } { 0 . 4 } } = 1 6 2 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } \ \mathrm { W } \qquad { \mathrm { A n s } } .
$$

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l } & { E = { \mathrm { E n e r g y } } { \mathrm { c o n s u m e d } } } \\ & { \qquad = { \frac { 6 5 \times 1 0 ^ { 3 } } { 1 0 0 0 } } \times 4 0 = 6 4 8 0 { \mathrm { ~ k W h } } . } \end{array} }

Example. 7.16 Two boilers one with a super heater and the other without a super heater are supplying equal quantities of steam into a common main. The temperature of steam from the boiler with super heater is 330°C and that of steam in the main is 260°C. If the pressure in the boiler and the main is 15 kg/cm2 and specific heat of superheated steam is 0.54 determine the quality of steam supplied by boiler without super heater.

Solution.

Let

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l } & { q \ = \mathrm { D r y n e s s ~ f r a c t i o n ~ o f ~ s t e a m ~ s u p p l i e d ~ b y ~ b o i l e r ~ w i t h o u t } } \\ & { \qquad \operatorname { s u p e r ~ h e a t e r } } \end{array} }
$$

At 15 $\mathrm { k g / c m ^ { 2 } }$ (From steam tables)

$$
t = { \mathrm { S a t u r a t i o n ~ t e m p e r a t u r e ~ o f ~ s t e a m } } = 1 9 7 . 4 ^ { \circ } { \mathrm { C } }
$$

$$
L = \mathrm { L a t e n t h e a t } = 4 6 6 . 7 \mathrm { k c a l }
$$

$$
H _ { w } = 2 0 0 . 7 \mathrm { k c a l }
$$

Let us assume that each boiler supplies one kg of steam into the common main.

$$
H ^ { \prime } = \mathrm { H e a t ~ o f ~ s t e a m } = H _ { w } + q L = 2 0 0 . 7 + q \times 4 6 6 . 7 8 \mathrm { ~ k c a l } .
$$

Now $t _ { s } =$ Temperature of super heated steam = 330°C

$$
C _ { p } = 0 . 5 4
$$

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l } & { H _ { s } = { \mathrm { H e a t ~ o f ~ s u p e r ~ h e a t e d ~ s t e a m } } = H + C _ { p } \left( t _ { s } - t \right) } \\ & { ~ } \\ & { ~ = 6 6 7 . 4 + 0 . 5 4 \left( 3 3 0 - 1 9 7 . 4 \right) { \mathrm { k c a l } } = 7 3 9 { \mathrm { ~ k c a l } } } \end{array} }
$$

$$
H _ { 1 } = H ^ { \prime } + H _ { \mathrm { s } } = \ : 2 0 0 . 7 + q \times 4 6 6 . 7 + 7 3 9 \ : \mathrm { k c a l } .
$$

where $H _ { 1 }$ is the heat of steam supplied by both the boilers

Since the temperature of steam in the common main is 260°C and saturation termperature is 197.4°C it is obvious that steam is still in super heated condition.

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l } & { H _ { 2 } = \operatorname { H e a t } \operatorname { o f } 2 \operatorname { k g } \operatorname { o f } \operatorname { s t e a m } \operatorname { i n } \operatorname { t h e } \operatorname* { m a i n } } \\ & { \qquad = [ H + C _ { p } ( t _ { s } - t ) ] \times 2 } \\ & { \qquad = [ 6 6 7 . 4 + 0 . 5 4 ( 2 6 0 - 1 9 7 . 4 0 ] \times 2 = 1 4 0 2 . 4 \operatorname { k c a l } . } \end{array} }
$$

Now

$$
H _ { 1 } = H _ { 2 }

$$

Example 7.17. Calculate the efficiency of a boiler in which coal consumption is 65 kg per hour and which generates 370 kg of steam per hour at 0.93 dryness fraction and at a pressure of 8 bar absolute. Coal used has the following composition per kg.

Carbon = 0.71   
Hydrogen = 0.05   
Oxygen = 0.11   
Sulphur = 0.02   
Ash = 0.11   
Feed water temperature = 24ºC

Solution.

P = Pressure of steam = 8 bar   
From steam tales hf = Sensible heat = 721 kJ/kg   
hfg = Latent heat of steam = 2046.5 kJ/kg   
x = Dryness fraction   
H = Heat of 1 kg of steam   
= hf + . hfg = 721 + 0.93 × 2046.5 = 2624.3 kJ/kg   
H<sub>1</sub> = Heat supplied to steam per kg   
= H  heat contained in 1 kg of feed water   
= 2624.3  1 × 4.18 × (24  0) = 2524 kJ/kg   
W = Weight of steam produced per hour = 370 kg   
H<sub>2</sub> = Heat of steam = W × H<sub>1</sub> = 370 × 2524 = 933880   
C = Calorific value of coal   
= 33800 C + 144000 <sup>0</sup> <sub>H </sub><sup></sup> 9270 S+   
8

where

$$
C = { \mathrm { A m o u n t ~ o f ~ h y d r o g e n ~ p e r ~ k g ~ o f ~ c o a l } } = 0 . 7 1
$$

$$
H = \mathrm { A m o u n t \ o f h y d r o g e n \ p e r \ k g \ o f \ c o a l = 0 . 0 5 }
$$

$$
O \ = \mathrm { A m o u n t \ o f \ o x y g e n \ p e r \ k g \ o f \ c o a l } = 0 . 1 1
$$

$$
S = { \mathrm { A m o u n t ~ o f ~ s u l p h u r ~ p e r ~ k g ~ o f ~ c o a l } } = 0 . 0 2
$$

$$
C _ { \mathrm { v } } = 3 3 8 0 0 \times 0 . 7 1 + 1 4 4 0 0 0 \left( 0 . 0 5 - { \frac { 0 . 1 1 } { 8 } } \right) + 9 2 7 0 \ + 0 . 0 2

$$
= 2 9 3 6 7 \mathrm { k J / k g }
$$

$$
W _ { 1 } = \mathrm { A m o u n t ~ o f ~ c o a l ~ b u r n t ~ p e r ~ h o u r } = 6 5 \mathrm { ~ k g }
$$

$$
H _ { 3 } = \mathrm { { T o t a l h e a t i n p u t } }
$$

$$
= C _ { v } \times W _ { 1 } = 2 9 3 6 7 . 4 \times 6 5 = \ 1 9 0 8 8 5 5 \mathrm { k J }

Example 7.18. A boiler working at a pressure of 10 bar generates 2100 kg of dry and saturated steam per hour. Example 7.19. Sketch and describe in brief a steam power plant indicating various parts of the plant.

Solution. In a steam power plant, fuel and air enter the power plant and products of combustion leave the unit. There is a transfer of heat to the cooling water, and work is done in the form of the electrical energy leaving the power plant. The overall objective of a power plant is to convert the availability (to do work) of the fuel into work (in the form of electrical energy) in the most efficient manner, taking into consideration cost, space, safety, and environmental concerns.

A schematic daigram of a steam power plant is shown in Fig. 7.55. High-pressure superheated steam leaves the boiler, which is also referred to as a steam generator, and enters the turbine. The steam expands in the turbine and, in doing so, does work, which enables the turbine to drive the electric generator. The low-pressure steam leaves the turbine and enters the condenser, where heat is transferred from the steam (causing it to condense) to the cooling.

Example 7.20. Determine the boiler efficiency if the boiler generates 23,000 kg of steam at 10.2 kg/cm2 dry and saturated. The amount of coal used is 2100 kg and the calorific value of coal is 8600 kcal/kg. The feed water temperature is $1 0 5 ^ { \circ } C$

Solution. Total heat of steam at 10.2 kg/cm2.

$$
= 6 6 4 \mathrm { k c a l / k g }
$$

$$
\begin{array} { c } { { \displaystyle \eta _ { b o i l e r } = \frac { 2 3 0 0 0 \left( 6 6 4 - 1 0 5 \right) } { 2 1 0 0 \times 8 6 0 0 } = 0 . 7 1 } } \\ { { \displaystyle = 7 { \bf 1 } \% \ s { \bf A } { \bf n } { \bf s } . } } \end{array}
$$

## QUESTIONS

1. How will you classify various types of boilers?

2. What is the difference between water-tube and fire-tube boilers? Describe the working principle of Cochran or Lancashire boilers.

3. Write short notes on the following: (a) Boiler mountings. (b) Boiler accessories. (c) Efficiency of a boiler.

4. What is a superheater? Describe different types of super-heaters.

5. State the advantages of superheated steam. Explain the working of a superheater.

6. Write short notes on the following. (a) Maintenance of a boiler. (b) Feed water treatment. (c) Feed water control.

7. Explain the methods used to increase thermal efficiency of a steam power plant.

8. Write short notes on the following: (a) pH value of water (b) Power plant pumps. (c) Comparison of forced and induced draft system for boilers.

9. Describe with a neat sketch, (a) water tube boiler, (b) fire tube boiler.

10. Describe a feed water regulator.

11. For a boiler, draw a flow diagram showing flue gas flow and water steam flow.

12. State the advantages of high pressure boilers.

13. Write short notes on the following: (a) Selection of boiler. (b) Gas fired boilers.

14. Discuss modern trends in generating steam.

15. Discuss modern trends in boilers.

16. Write short notes on the following: (a) Economiser (b) Hydraulic test of a boiler.

17. Describe the systematic arrangement in a modern steam power station and detail the various heat saving devices used.

18. What are the advantages of using water tube boilers and what are the special characteristics which enable water tube boilers best suited for modern power plant?

19. What are the high pressure boilers and how they differ in construction and working principle from ordinary boilers? What are the advantages gained by forced water circulation?

20. Describe construction and working of La Mont, Loeffler, Benson and Velox boilers giving suitable sketches.

21. What is the function of a superheater in a power plant?

22. Describe advantages gained by using economizers in a modern power plant.

23. What are the main types of air heaters employed in a steam power plant? Describe the regenerative air heater.

24. (a) Why is the feed water treatment necessary before it is supplied to the boiler? (b) What are the effects of impurities in feed water on the boiler?

25. Describe different methods used for feed water treatment.

26. Write short notes on the following: (a) Internal water treatment. (b) External treatment of feed water. (c) Chemical treatment of feed water. (d) Steam purity.

27. What is the function of a steam generator? Write down its main components.

28. How does an industrial boiler differ from a power plant boiler?

29. Explain the characteristic features of a water tube boiler. How is it different from a fire tube boiler?

30. Explain the following boiler mountings in brief: (a) Fusible plug. (b) Spring loaded safety valve. (c) Blow off cock. (d) Water level indicator.

31. What is circulation in a boiler ? What is the difference between natural circulation and forced circulation?

32. (a) Why is too much steaming not desired in a riser tube? (b) Why should no moisture flow along with steam from the drum to the superheater? (c) What is blow-down? Why is it needed?

33. (a) What are the function of the steam drum in a water tube boiler? (b) What do you mean by primary and foaming?

35. What are once-through boilers? How do they differ from drum boilers?

36. Explain the functions of primary air and secondary air?

37. What is super-critical boilers? What are its merits and demerits?

38. Write short notes on: (a) Pendant superheater. (b) Desuperheater. (c) Tilting burners. (d) Feed water softening

39. (a) How is the erosion rate of fly ash related to gas velocity. (b) Where is reheater located? (c) How is the water level in steam drum controlled?

40. What are the major difference between mountings and accessories? Give five examples of each?

41. Define draught and name different methods of producing draught.

42. What do you understand by natural draught? What are its limitations?

43. Explain the principles used in forced and induced draughts. Discuss the merits and demerits of each over the other.

44. List out the merits of mechanical draught over natural draught.

45. What do you understand by steam jet draught? Explain its working principle. Where is it used?

46. Name various draught systems? Describes the operation of a balanced draught system.

47. Name the different types of chimneys used. State the advantages of steel chimney.

48. What are the harmful effects caused by using impure water in boilers? Describe the various methods of purifying feed water.

49. What is meant by make up water of boiler and how is this water fed into a boiler?

50. (a) What are the advantages gained by using superheated steam? (b) Describe the various factors which determine the location of a steam power station.

51. State the advantages and disadvantages of a steam power station as compared to hydroelectric power station and nuclear power station.

52. Write short notes on the following: (a) Hydraulic test of a boiler. (b) Draught fans. (c) Steam separator. (d) Heat flow in steam plant.

53. What are natural draft and mechanical draft? How is the latter more advantageous? What is the utility of balanced draft? How is the balanced draft produced?

54. Describe the main types of fans used for production of draft in the boilers. What is the fields of application of each type?

55. What do you understand by draught ? How the draughts are classified?

56. (a) What are the limitations of chimney draught? (b) Discuss the merits and demerits of forced draught over induced draught. (c) Why balanced draught is preferred over forced or induced draught?

57. Draw a neat diagram of a volex boiler and discuss its merits and demerits with Benson boiler.

58. (a) What do you understand by supercharged boiler? (b) What are the considerations in locating the superheater and economiser?

59. (a) What is the necessity of a soot blower? (b) How is the slag removed from a boiler?

60. Write short notes on: (a) Boiler trial (b) Boiler balance sheet (c) Boiler maintenance (d) Boiler inspection.
